## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: plasticity theory
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling stress (sigma) as a function of strain (epsilon) and temperature (T), which is a common scenario in plasticity theory, particularly in the context of material deformation and creep.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Euler's equation: sigma = E * epsilon (linear elastic response)
- Poisson's equation: sigma = E * (1 - v) * epsilon (linear elastic response with Poisson's ratio)
- Gibbs free energy: sigma = d(epsilon) * (delta(epsilon)) (thermodynamic force and driving force)
- Neumann's law of change of state: d sigma / d t = k / (T**2) * (sigma - sigma_equilibrium) (relaxation to equilibrium)
- power-law creep: sigma = A * (epsilon / epsilon_0)**n * exp(-Q / (k_B * T)) (creep deformation under constant stress)
- Saint-Venant's principle: sigma = (E / (1 - v^2)) * (epsilon + (1 - v) * epsilon_normalized) (plane stress problem)
- Arrhenius equation for creep: k = k_0 * exp(-Q / (k_B * T)) (reaction rate and temperature dependence)
- temperature-dependent Young's modulus: E = E_0 * (1 + c1 * T) (Young's modulus as a function of temperature)
- inhomogeneous deformation: sigma = E * epsilon + E_t * epsilon_t (two-phase material or inhomogeneous deformation)
- non-Newtonian viscosity: sigma = tau * (d epsilon / d x) (non-Newtonian fluid viscosity)
- Cosserat theory: sigma = lambda * I_1 + 2 * mu * I_2 (continuum mechanics with Cosserat effects)
- temperature-dependent flow stress: sigma = sigma_0 + k * exp(-Q / (k_B * T)) (temperature-dependent flow stress in high-temperature plasticity)
- mixed-mode deformation: sigma = E * epsilon + E_t * epsilon_t + lambda * epsilon_norm (mixed-mode deformation of composite materials)
- ductile damage evolution: sigma = (1 - D) * E * epsilon + (1 - (1 - D) * E) * epsilon_t (ductile damage evolution equation)
- viscoelastic response: sigma = E * epsilon + E_t * epsilon_t (viscoelastic behavior of polymers)
- Pseudo-Hamilton principle: delta sigma = E * epsilon + (E / (1 - v^2)) * (epsilon_normalized) (Pseudo-Hamilton principle for elastic solids)
- non-isothermal viscoelasticity: sigma = (E / (1 - v^2)) * (epsilon + epsilon_norm) + E_t * epsilon_t (non-isothermal viscoelastic behavior)
- Fracture mechanics: sigma = sigma_c * (a / W) ** (1/2) (stress intensity factor and fracture toughness)
- Prestress: sigma = sigma_st + sigma_ss * cos(2 * pi * t / T) (prestress for thermoplastic materials)
- inhomogeneous plasticity: sigma = (E / (1 - v^2)) * (epsilon + epsilon_norm) + E_p * epsilon_p (inhomogeneous plasticity model)
- microplasticity: sigma = E * epsilon + E_p * epsilon_p (microplasticity model in porous materials)
- complete damage model: sigma = (E / (1 - v^2)) * (epsilon + epsilon_norm) + E_p * epsilon_p (complete damage model with temperature and strain rate dependence)
- split Hopkinson pressure bar: sigma = k_1 * t * epsilon^p + k_2 * t * epsilon^h (plastic strain wave propagation and split Hopkinson pressure bar)
- Kolsky stress bar: sigma = E_0 * epsilon * exp(-k * t) (stress relaxation in Kolsky bar)
- antiplane stress: sigma = lambda * I_1 + mu * I_2 (antiplane stress and strain in non-polarized materials)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- temperature dependence → Arrhenius equation, exponential dependence, Gaussian envelope
- non-Newtonian behavior → power-law, rational fraction, and Coupling with strain rate and temperature
- creep → power-law, exponential dependence, cosine and sine envelope
- ductile damage → rational fraction, and power-law dependence on strain and temperature
- antiplane stress → combination of lambda * I_1 and mu * I_2, piecewise functions, and finite differences
- mixed-mode deformation → power-law, and combination of linear and nonlinear functions
- Pseudo-Hamilton principle → combination of elastic and viscoelastic behavior, exponential dependence, and rational fraction
- non-isothermal viscoelasticity → combination of temperature-dependent elastic and viscoelastic behavior, and rational fraction
- prestress → cosine and sine envelope, and combination of constant and time-dependent terms
- Kolsky stress bar → combination of exponential decay, and linear and rational fraction dependence on time
- split Hopkinson pressure bar → power-law, and combination of linear and nonlinear functions
- inhomogeneous plasticity → combination of linear and nonlinear functions, and exponential dependence on strain and temperature
- microplasticity → combination of linear and nonlinear functions, and exponential dependence on strain and temperature
- complete damage model → combination of temperature-dependent elastic and viscoelastic behavior, and rational fraction
- temperature-dependent viscoelasticity → combination of temperature-dependent elastic and viscoelastic behavior, and rational fraction
